    \n I soft-cancelled our Night Witches game tonight (this would be our 5th session, moving to the third duty station and maybe our first MC switch, depending). I say soft-cancelled because I said I couldn't host, knowing that would inevitably lead to it not happening for a variety of reasons. To be honest, I'm just feeling anxious and disconnected and not wanting to be around people, but I also do miss the game, which has been going really well so far. We usually get together on Saturdays too (well, an overlapping but not identical set of people) and play board games. If I'm not feeling the same at that time, I may propose we try out InSpectres or something one-shotty.

    Did you make up a new oracle for the setting? The Quiet Year is maybe my favorite game of all time.

    \n\nApril 2016 \n

    \n
    \n I've been playing Final Fight, Castlevania: Bloodlines and a selection of random video games of the 16-bit era for an hour or two each day.

    On Friday I'll be hosting a boardgame night at a local pub. It's a regular weekly thing that I'm using to reconnect locally (I moved back to Upper Savo after three years away just recently). I'm expecting a bunch of middle schoolers, a couple hardcore gamers and maybe some regulars from the pub; the gaming will be light to midweight German boardgames, probably starting with Modern Art and continuing with e.g. Arena.

    Depending on the participants on Friday, we might continue a discussions regarding roleplaying plans for the summer season. The three big propositions on the table are playtest for my own project, a full campaign of Ars Magica, and a new, fresh old school D&D sandbox. Just planning stages for now on all of them.

Then I sprinted across town to the Vampire LARP. Can Scunthorpe and Grimsby be signatories to the vampire peace treaty despite their unusual social arrangements? This still hangs in the balance!

    I endorse this thread and demand more like it.

    \n Saturday: the penultimate session of a long-running 13th Age campaign, which has been fun but I'm looking forward to the series of one-shots and then potentially a Fellowship campaign to come.

    Tuesday: Night Witches, Duty Station 5, with me rotating back into the MC slot. I introduced a new Commissar, Pilar Illyichina Strelkova i Rodrigues, daughter of a Russian expatriate in Spain. She has very strong ideas on how lack of discipline and treason caused the downfall of the Republic.

    (And yup, we've run this from Duty Station 1; I previously GM'ed Duty Station 3. Most of us are on our original character, take that as you will--in my case, it's because my Vera has determined that she will live out the war and has taken steps--like always being in command--to ensure that. And earning a chestful of medals in the meantime!)

    Tonight: Dracula Dossier, almost certainly the last session of the very long 1894 section. I'm looking forward to bringing back my Eternal Lies PC in the 1940 section...

    \n Eero,

    How do you invite people to your boardgame night? Is it a small, friendly thing, or are you renting out tables at a bar and advertising to strangers?
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
  • \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n\nEero_Tuovinen \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nApril 2016 \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    Friday I tried to get my GM-less Dramasystem hack test-campaign going, but alas, someone had to cancel so the rest of us played boardgames. Between Two Cities is a fine boardgame.
    \nIt is pretty palatable, yes. I've got it in my selection for tomorrow's game night, too.\n
    How do you invite people to your boardgame night? Is it a small, friendly thing, or are you renting out tables at a bar and advertising to strangers?
    \nThe context is that this is something I've been doing for years, in different forms. I use the boardgaming as a hiring system for rpgs (easier to get people to join in boardgames, generally speaking, and they allow me to test the mettle of prospective roleplayers), alongside enjoying it for its own sake.

    The current set-up originated last year: I was still living in Helsinki, but I came to Upper Savo for six weeks to do some seasonal forestry in the fall, which gave me an opportunity to strike. I asked my teenaged nephew (he's like 14 years old this year maybe?) to get some of his friends together for a bit of boardgaming then. I conducted a couple boardgaming nights with them, taught some games and table etiquette, and left them with instructions to continue playing weekly over the winter.

    When I came back in the spring, they'd been fumbling along with boardgames, but hadn't developed the social capital much, so I took to it again. I moved the meetings to Fridays at my sister's restaurant, as Fridays have been much too quiet there lately, and asked my gaming friends (the few who still live here - I've been away for three years, and Upper Savo is the kind of area where people come from, not where they go to) to join in. I also prepared to invite in any interested customers; the clientele of the restaurant runs a gamut from alcoholics to families, so you never know who might show up, and what they might like.

    Last Friday we had three children courtesy of my nephew, one of my old gaming friends and one other person, I think - six in total. This Friday the gamers will probably show up in greater force (2-4 maybe?), and I expect about five-ish children; would make the arrangements easier if I could split the children and the adults into their own tables. We'll see how it goes.

    But no, I haven't done any particular advertising on this yet, as I've just started doing it actively again. I will maybe put up some posters or something at the local high school and so on sooner or later. Then again, summer holidays are starting, and I don't actually need that large of a crew for now. Perhaps next fall, when the schools start, I'll see about starting to develop the ranks and quality with an eye towards games like Diplomacy and such.

    Regarding the bar thing, although in this case I have a personal in on the space thanks to my sister owning the place, I haven't found it difficult to make similar arrangements with other restaurants or bars, either. Most of them around here are happy enough with boardgamers wanting to play there - they strive to be public rooms, after all.
    \n
    \n
    \n

    \n\nRafu \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nApril 2016 \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    I didn't play anything this week. I haven't played anything since early March. How can I think about design if I'm not playing?
    \nAs a matter of fact you can. But there are some specific pitfalls you need to avoid, I believe. Which boil down to design as a substitute for play vs. actually designing toward future play. When you take real people - the actual players - out of your thought process, you're usually left with pretty poor design.
    \n
    \n
    \n

    \n
    \n I ran the 20th game of our 5e old school dungeon crawling game set in post-apocalyptic Europe! It was a quiet-ish game, no hirelings lost and no PCs had a near-death experience, since they went for a dungeon a bit below their level. Burrowing wasps, a mimic, and robotic zombies in a half-flooded office complex on the Romanian shore of the Black Sea. But one PC finally hit level 5! Peter's Annette is a now proudly a 5th level Human Child Scavenger (Archaeologist), and at long last has her second combat drone.

    I also hosted and ran a Passover Seder for the first time, which felt strangely similar to GMing.

    \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nApril 2016 \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n GMed Night Witches which got very dark. Maybe too dark. I...have to talk to folks next Tuesday.

    Dracula Dossier 1894 wrapped last week with Liesl spending an evening at the opera (Faust, natch) with Dracula, the fairies of Misslewaith Manor turning out to be mi-go, and Liesl rejecting Dracula's offer to learn about the darkness at his side.

    And last night's Primetime Adventures California '70s noir went nicely. Dudley Moore (!) sued paparazzo Leo Main and my PI Sam(antha) was called in to testify against Leo, her ex-husband. We had a bunch of nice flashbacks showing how their marriage collapsed. Meanwhile, alcoholic cop Tommy and Black Panther fugitive Honeysuckle formed an odd couple investigation team, driving down to Long Beach to followup on the recent drug-based murders of local strippers.

    \n For Tabletop Day, I facilitated Microscope at the games gathering at the local bookstore. This started with the Game-of-Thrones-style warring noble houses seed from Microscope Explorer, and concluded with the legalisation of marriage between humans and lizardfolk. The Microscope novice at the table started out by saying "so, what's the combat system?" and ended by saying saying, "wow, this is great, we made so much in two hours."
    \n

    \n\nHegar \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nMay 2016 \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n Nothing but Blades in the Dark! I've been running it with a semi-revolving group who are either completely new to RPGs or returning after 10+ year hiatuses (hiati? :P). At first everyone was focused entirely on the score and being professional. Then the session before last, the lurk decided to gather info on the slide during downtime - just as the slide over-indulged and bragged about the crew's last score! After the slide walked into the secret lair, high and with floosy in-tow a very exciting confrontation ensued - the result was the slide paying 1 coin to the group and getting a Ghost Pact never to blab about the crew again, while the Lurk left duskvol for a while with one of the rooks.

    During this session's downtime the spider responsible for the Ghost Pact needed a coin. The slide offered him one, but then said actually he'd only do it in exchange for removing the pact. The slide's player is very new to RPGs - we all thought he just didn't understand that the Pact couldn't hurt him unless he let it, but it seemed like a fair enough deal so it went ahead. Then the slide asks, "Do I need to use a downtime action to go tell the billhooks where our secret liar is?" Brilliant.
    \n

    \n\nericvulgaris \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nMay 2016 \n edited May 2016
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n Typically I play one shots, but I've been transitioning to more longer form gameplay: All but my Burning Wheel game can be found online at my youtube.

    A recent shift in my work starting time, the break between the end of Season 2 and Season 3 of my one shot show Once Upon A Game, and my family visiting has meant I've been playing less than usual.

    HOWEVER-- things are on the up and up again and here's what I've been up to:

    The Quiet Year with 2 new friends who never played TQY before! We did a standard post-apocalyptic setting but made it on a mountain. Cool things discovered were a creepy radio tower, a legendary lake monster, and purple ore. The three of us had a blast although we sort of rushed the ending... boy that game takes a long time. I think I very much prefer the shorter version where you play fewer cards per season.

    The Burning Wheel is my only IRL game. We wrapped up a completed Night Witches campaign and a player was very excited to do a Town Watch campaign drawing heavily from Deadwood and The Wire. We spoke about a system. Originally this was gonna be D&D 5e, but I let him borrow a copy of Burning Wheel Gold to look over and fell in love with it at once. So far we've only burned characters. I'll be playing an exiled, one-eye'd elf. I'm drawing a lot of inspiration from Detective Lester Freamon from The Wire. Troubled and eccentric, but has been in this town for a long time and knows it well. He's natural police.

    Night Witches starting from Duty Station 1 online. As the GM I'm taking the game in a direction that involves things that I didn't focus a lot on during my previous campaign of Night Witches. I'm looking more at rationing free time as well as the politics of the chain of command. It's been very fun! But also very dark and rough. 2/3 of the players characters did not make it to Duty Station 2. Let this be a lesson about taking regard for your plane and you crashing it!

    Blades in the Dark for players all brand new to Blades. We settled on the Vigilante crew-type by Sean Nittner! Because this campaign is has a limited number of sessions, we spent a lot of time in character creation talking about what our goals will be for this campaign! We've settled on tackling some of the corruption in the city and, in particular, taking down the Circle of Flame who are a bunch of nefarious artifact collectors. I love the name my players came up with: CLOAK & GAVEL.

    D&D 5e: Winters Edge A good friend of mine is running a 5e campaign about colonization/frontiers set in the thawing north. I'm playing a Warlock with the patron of a neutral grim reaper like demigod. It's fun learning why I got my power and why this demigod has chosen me and how it's affecting my relationships with my party members and our colony! This is not a very traditional D&D experience. Because we're playing online and each episode is streamed, a lot has been modified: The GM has combined a lot of the Kingdom management rules from Pathfinder into this game and the GM is coordinating with the audience concerning NPCs, and "tavern roleplay" like sessions keeping the world dynamic and interactive for EVERYONE. Super cool.

    Upcoming games that I'm also super excited about are: Blades Against Darkness which is a hack of Blades in the Dark inspired by Robert E Howard. With Once Upon A Game returning, you can also expect to see this month: Fiasco, The Skeletons and Shock.
    \n
    \n

    \n\nAdam_Dray \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nMay 2016 \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n Another session of my Pathfinder game where I'm playing my "Julia," an efrit bard 5/swashbuckler 3 played up from 1st level for the last year or so, based on Julie d'Aubigny.

    Her moral character is being tested (proved). They're delving underground to understand more and eventually tackle "The Thing That Devours." To learn more, they had to strike a devil's bargain with an ancient derro wizard. This involved giving the wizard blood, spit, skin, fingernails, hair, and so on--components which will the wizard will ultimately use to make a tiny homunculus of Julia, who will certainly be subjected to all kinds of torture in the wizard's people-ant-farm.

    Anyway, she learned that The Thing That Devours is some kind of banished elder god and that, as it devours parts of the bodies of the hobgoblins who live down here, it gains control over them.

    There a weird moment when Joe, playing an allegedly Lawful Good cleric, kept going on about how we should sacrifice the three hobgoblin NPCs who were helping us to the elder god, and I asked Joe, "What's your character's alignment?" with a certain amount of incredulity. Later, when he kept doing that, the GM asked the same thing. The table generally agreed that he wasn't playing LG. Especially the player of the dwarf, who is chaotic neutral. My hope is that the group doesn't fight about alignment as players, but I welcome intraparty bickering about the moral course of action.

    Julia also argued that we didn't have to be the heroes that save the world alone--especially if it looks like we have to do terrible, evil things to accomplish it "alone." She suggested that we could go to the local monarch and enlist help, because she suspected that monarchs listen when you talk about waking up elder gods who want to devour everything.
    \n

    \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
    \n
    \n\nMay 2016 \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n
    \n@Adam_Dray, glad to see another person who has made a Pathfinder bard based on Julie d'Aubigny! (Mine was swashbuckler archetype bard; I think I took Perform: Action Movie Quip as one of my skills. On the other hand, she was Neutral Evil and so had fewer moral quandaries.)

    Also, your cleric Joe sounds very much like a Joe I played with who also liked allegedly Lawful Good clerics and paladins...you aren't near Columbus Ohio, are you?

    Tonight should be my last GMing session of Night Witches; I expect to close out Duty Station 5 and then bring back Captain Vera for the end of the war. In my GM runs I've done a lot of experimenting with the politruks, because you can have fun playing against type. The three I used:

    1) Captain Nadezhda Toropova, a twenty-something woman whom I described as a "Komsomol camp counselor in way over her head." (Her motto would have been something like "Our goal is Socialism, our weapon is Education!") She was naive and ended profoundly disillusioned.

    2) Senior Lieutenant Olga, Nadia's assistant. She was Bolshevik before there were Bolsheviks--she and her husband had been sent to the camps by the Tsar after the 1905 Revolution, and she was proud to have disowned her emigre son. She tried to convince one PC to join SMERSH among other horrible things (including making said PC pull the trigger in a mock execution that only Olga knew was mock.)

    3) Senior Lieutenant Pilar Ililichyna Strelkova i Rodrigues, the current zampolit. She's half Spanish and witnessed the fall of the Republic first hand, which has made her a strict believer in doctrine and discipline. Things have not gone well with the PCs under her...

      \n\nCaesar Slaad \n\n\n

      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I went to International Tabletop Gameday at the FLGS, hoping to play the advertised D&D game with some friends. But the DM didn't show. So I pulled out Dungeons of Fate and Fate Accelerated an ran a quick impromptu dungeon adventure, followed by one of my friends running the "Red Packet Rumble" for Feng Shui 2.

      Both of these games had new adherents by the end of the session. Other than my friends, there was a father-and-son in the Dungeons of Fate game; he said that he ran RIFTS at home for his son but didn't really like the system. By the end of the game, he grabbed a box of Fate dice from the store and had ordered Fate Accelerated to play at home. And a friend that dropped in on the Feng Shui session said it was the best RPG he ever played and we are looking at starting a weeknight "small press RPG"* thing at the store soon!

      * - Small press meaning not WotC in this context.

      \n This past week, I played the "prep for 1940 Dracula Dossier by obsessively working with my notes" and realized I was as prepped as can be before this week's character creation session. I also played the "edit the Delta Green scenario I played in at GenCon and go 'Oh, that's what was going on!'" game, and Saturday, the real life larp "our apartment is getting everyone's backed up sh*t?!" which, fortunately, ended well, thanks to the superintendent, although the sequel game involved a fair bit of cleaning and bleach. Oh, and somewhere in there, I fit prepping to playtest one of the new Gumshoe Confidential single player and GM scenarios, or at least the "reading the scenario" step. Rereading the rules would help.

      Tomorrow, we might be playing Diaspora, wherein my PC will continue to throw up his hands and try to keep human civilization from self destructing and wonder why he is bothering. Oh yes, this involved authorizing folks to nuke his home planet if they deem it necessary, to keep a de-volution plague from spreading.

      \nEden at Story Games Seattle. Narwhals and bunnies try to explain reproduction to the innocent humans. Narwhals are convinced it is essential to sing together and have a magnificent horn, or else it won\u2019t work. Poor humans have no magnificent horn or lovely songs, so they are doomed to failure.

      Bunnies are convinced that sex always makes more bunnies, regardless of the species involved. Carpets of agitated rabbits give eager advice. \u201cI mean sure, you could do it too, but I'm telling ya you\u2019ll just get more bunnies!!!!!!\u201d

      The owl knows better.

      \n
      \n After the aforementioned tabletop gameday thing, I ran a short Feng Shui 2 intro at the FLGS with the new player who played it at gameday. It was fun, though I must say that some players just don't get the melodramatic archetype thing. Still, it's not my job to make the characters, so I rolled with it. Much butt-kicking fun was had. I am supposed to pull in a few more new players (one who currently isn't into role playing, one who is suffering through what I gather is a badly run D&D game) next week.

      I don't feel like Feng Shui 2 is suited to long term gaming, but I hope to let the newer players cut their teeth on it before moving on to something a little more serious.

      \n\nSimon_Pettersson \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I played Ribbon Drive. It was nice! It went better than last time we played it. I think I knew more how to make a playlist that works for the game. Not sure how well we did in taking cues from the music, though.

      Four colleagues, not wanting to move to Chicago when their company gets bought, take the severance pay and decide on a whim to go to Rio. Richard wanted to forget his wife and his life. Wayne wanted to escape the lie he was living. Jessie didn't really want to go, but wanted to prove to herself and her parents that she was free and a grown-up. Popcorn wanted to find herself.

      In the end, they all had to come to terms with who they were and how things were and they couldn't change things by going on a trip to Rio. But they managed to get some new perspectives and all, in their own ways, managed to let go.

      \n

      \n\nDavid_Berg \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I went to Camp Nerdly, so I got to play a bunch of stuff!

      The New World -- clash of characters at a meeting of cultures between natives, newcomers, and outsiders. For us, that meant fairies (Midsummer Night's Dream style), Irish peasants, and crusaders.

      Cartwheel shuttle crash on the Moon (not sure of proper name) -- tie strings to things by flashlight before your characters run out of air LARP.

      Fellowship PbtA epic fantasy adventure with a dwarf made of stone, a giant who was basically Groot, the heir of the cat-people, a reckless badass orc, and a prophet of doom traitor to our enemy. We killed a bunch of ice monsters in bizarrely colorful ways.

      Within My Clutches, playtest of my supervillain snafus game, with two deliriously sleep-deprived adult and one supers-almanac 10-year-old. Gold-creating alien Jack London earned U.S. citizenship by bribing Orrin Hatch.

      Don't Walk in Prince William Wood creepy storytelling around a campfire.

      Even more interesting is that it was the first time GMing for one of our group, meaning I got to play under someone of my lineage, as it were. And that was most excellent of all!

      \n Currently, I'm playing the "if I revive the Kerberos game, what system do we use" game. Previously, we used Kerberos Fate, which was a blast, but we had some issues even at the time. OTOH, while I love FAE, three of the four players don't want it for Kerberos, and they may have a point. I'm trying to cram Atomic Robo Fate into my head, as Aviatrix and one of the Kerberos players pretty much agree it should be able to handle things like this.

      \n\n2097 \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n edited May 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I played D&D! Finally real RPGs (sorry, Pandemic Legacy -- but we'll get back to you tomorrow) for the first time since 2015! I've been sick and when I got on my feet I got back into Magic cards after a decade long lapse.
      But tonight! We were one player short of Pandemic Legacy so we just jumped into chargen and the intro adventure of Curse of Strahd.
      Party got eaten by wolves and died. GREAT SESSION!!!!
      Got compliments from the group, feeling really good about RPGs again. The insp was flying, the flashlights were falling. Lots of RP, lots of ten-foot-pole pokery, lots of very dungeon worldy fights, the best from my players yet with shoving and using the environment and describing their actions in a varied and creative way. I've ran the real DW with a party that was just "I transform into a bear again" every combat (when I played it I made a point of being as many different weird and useless animals as possible).
      So DW itself isn't panacea. But here they made great use of the environment, earning advantage etc. I've described this as a great strength of 5e but one that has come out more at con games than my home game. But tonight was the night apparently! So great. All credit to my wonderful group who really brought their best to bring it alive.

      So amazing. Is there a spoiler block on S-G? I could paste in the session report from TPB.
      \n

      \n\nCaesar Slaad \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Last night - Next session of the Feng Shui 2 into adventure; this time we ran it for one new player and one player who had only played 3.5.

      The new player took the Big Bruiser archetype and made his character a demigod; he wanted to use a character called Kratos from the video game God of War as a model. I told him he could just style his attacks as divine powered.

      The previously 3.5 player made a driver named Corbin Dallas who won an all expenses paid trip to Hong Kong, but found out the trip was a sham and still doesn't know why.

      We only had time for one fight. It's funny how every time I run this scenario, it's so different. Corbin Dallas faced a bulk of the bad guys alone in the parking lot with his car, but Kratos took the mooks in the ground out en masse by tossing a hospital bed at them.

      Today was a quick Shadow of the Century (Fate Core) playtest, using a group of Buckaroo Banzi like pregenerated characters from the book.

      Tomorrow is Pathfinder. Lotta gaming going on...

      \nFiasco with the high school playset. We start off *very* out-of-bounds and then the game improves considerably as we continuously tone things down in play, focus more on the characters as people (albeit people with overhead compartments full of baggage). Its ends up less 50 Shades of Grey and more Freaks & Geeks meets Breakfast Club, thank god.

      Also, the sweet nerdy kids explain that sexy jackalopes are not in the Monster Manual.

      \n Started a new campaign with my weekly group last week, using a PbtA hack of Night's Black Agents. I'm using the Dracula Dossier, but my players think they're in a straight-up modern espionage game. They just got their hands on a keycard to a safe deposit box in London that contains the unredacted Dracula.

      I would not normally drop a game-changer like this on my players without buy-in, but I know them well enough to know that they will eat it up. Can't wait to see their reactions. Mua ha ha.

      \nBurning Wheel Our town watch has a murder on our hands. A dwarf body was found bruised and beaten. Left on a skiff on the river. It looks racially motivated. My one eyed elf is getting too old for this....

      Blades in the Dark CLOAK & GAVEL member Blink was tasked by his old gang to take out an Inspector. They succeeded but did so amidst the chaos of a gang war and generated about 8 heat. Little do they know that Inspector was on the take from some powerful patrons...

      D&D Our northern settlement formally met with the dwarven kingdoms in the mountainhomes. What was once a "take care of some Duergar" turned into "Oh got the Duergar are 100% communists and fulfilled some prophecy and this is too much, PEACE". In the meantime we're dealing with our homefront after a natural disaster (glacial flood) did some damage and politics down south may mean we're short our mercenary company.

      Blades Against Darkness Gwala, the Ush'dvanian renegade found solace from the torment of losing his wife and child in the company of his friends... for a little while. Gwala plots to amass enough wealth to restore his wife's soul to the land of the living and they be reunited---- as long as Gwala survives our next incursion into the obsidian powerplants deep in the volcanic basin called the Ashlands.

      \n\n2097 \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n We scheduled Curse of Strahd tomorrow and played Pandemic Legacy tonight.

      My goal in coop games is to be supportive of everyone and let everyone contribute. But one player made a choice that was very clearly... destructive for all of us, and in a way that affects the rest of the campaign going forward. I... could've handled it better, I got passive aggressive, making jokes, and also trying to take deep breaths but I was visibly upset. I mean... it's such a small thing. Who cares if we win or lose this campaign. I just get really invested. [He made it so that one of the characters became pretty much unusable for the rest of the campaign in a situation where he could've gotten away with a very minor scar.]

      We should've stopped him, paid more attention and I think that that was the problem. We have three nerds around the board doing like topology analysis of viral pathways and statistics calculation on the infection rate and this guy he's still asking basic rules questions. I've got to learn to be more patient and supportive. He is my friend.\u2665
      He ain't heavy, he's my co-player!

      I behaved really badly tonight. I wasn't the only one, the other two nerds joined in. That doesn't make it better, it makes it worse.
      \n

      \n\nmilesgaborit \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n edited May 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n First, on Wednesday, I ran the 2nd session of Blades in the Dark with the group of 11-12 year olds. We didn't get much done in the 1st session last week - chargen was a little more fiddly than I expected, having gotten used to comparatively chill PbtA games like the Warren lately, and the kids spent a lot of time picking their initial hideout upgrades.

      This week's session was fantastic though! We're playing through the quickstart setup, with the Clockwork Falcons (our protagonists) having taken a job to burglarize the headquarters (and sword-fighting school!) of the Red Sash gang. Things went splendidly haywire, abetted by each of the kids' attempts to shoehorn in special abilities - like, they wanted to use their special powers so bad that they didn't care how non-applicable they were to the situation at hand. Fun!

      I'm also really liking how Blades sits kind of at the mechanical intersection of PbtA and Burning Wheel. Fiction in-fiction out play + negotiated approach, difficulty, and stakes = big fun and really surprising outcomes! Wishing now that I'd shelled out for book during the Blades kickstarter, rather than just the pdf.

      Then, tonight, I get to play Apocalypse World for the first time in like 4 years. Going to use the 2nd Edition playbooks and revised moves. And I actually get to play rather than MC! I'm thinking of going with the Child-Thing playbook, but the Water Bearer is also looking pretty hot.
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nHouse of Reeds at Story Games Seattle. Our house is the ship that carries us between the stars, to bring our carnival of mystery and wonder to new and unsuspecting planets.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\n2097 \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Curse of Strahd playing wildly.

      As per the rules, I checked for random encounters every 30 minutes. That's every sixth \xbc-mile hex. Random encounters trigger on 18, 19 or 20 on the check d20. They didn't get a single one after 25 checks! Last session they were killed by wolves after just stepping outside the first village!
      They did get one 18+ roll, and the encounter table showed that it was only a trinket, I rolled that it was the flag from a ship at sea -- perfect because one of the characters was a sailor looking for his ship.

      But we played for five hours and they avoided everything !!! And we checked off many of the interesting RP moments (which were handled beautifully by my group, they did great) and I handed out levels like candy because I do not understand the level/xp system in CoS.
      \n
      \n

      \n\nRafu \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Finished a second game of The Truth Dies with Them! The first one we started, actually. This time, we got another one out of the three possible classes of endings \u2014 I have yet to see a "failure" ending (the one where the truth does actually die with them).
      \n

      \nFellowship Arkona, Lady Twilight, ex-Queen of the Elves rides (on a unicorn) again! An interesting setup with the heir being the scion of Turan, the empire of builders. (I don't know Turandot the opera that well, but now I'm anticipating using opera-derived nomenclature for the Turanian empire.) We fought a torb! The system absolutely sings.

      13th Age the much-delayed finale to our campaign (which has gone on some two years at this point--it shocked me to realize it's been that long since I was the regular GM for that group.) Some interesting fights, but I'm kinda glad we're moving on now.

      Didn't play it, but I finished writing the Trail of Cthulhu scenario I've pledged to run at Dexcon. Now to see if I can playtest it a couple of times before the con...

      \n\n2097 \n\n\n

      \n\nJune 2016 \n edited June 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n My Curse of Strahd group consists of three [including me as DM] of the four participants in the Pandemic Legacy campaign. So when the rest of us were early, we whipped out CoS and played for an hour. Still no fights. And... well, I'm super happy with the session and I think we're at rocket fuel town it's so good, but... we have this one player who really wants to engage with the fighting mechanics (was the feedback last time). And since we didn't this time... it was all talking scenes, investigating, exploring...
      Since they were in a city, there were no random encounter rules either.
      Edit: This time around, I got very nice feedback and compliments from that player! Makes me feel great


      So this was literally a "not a single die roll was made" session. Now, Adam Koebel said on YouTube that he hates that, he hates bothering with a game if the mechanics aren't helping you... but... the mechanics are helping me, except that they are "invisible". The mechanics that came into this game was A. Prep (mechanic: "read the module") and B. Petitioner/Granter from DramaSystem/Unframed. I used the heck out of this with very satisfying results.


      Then the fourth Pandemic Legacy player showed up and we played two missions, early and late August (we won late August). Both games were much faster than normal. We typically take a little more for half an hour and teardown (and this doesn't scale, we take this long for every game even in a marathon session) and an hour for the actual game part. This time, the setup/teardown took as long as normal but the games were much shorter. The first we died really quickly. And the other we won really quickly.


      Pandemic Legacy is satisfying mechanically (interesting combo building, maths etc) but I'm very disappointed in the story. So it's the opposite to CoS for me right now, where I love how the players are picking sides and starting fights in the various villages of Barovia but we have a dearth of player-visible mechanics.(Edit: Which turned out to be fine after all. Great!)

      \n Played The Final Girl for the first time. Overall went pretty well. We didn't define the killer as well as we should have, and that led to some bizarre tonal discord and a story that didn't hang together super well, thematically or logically. We also had 7 players, and it is generally my experience that larger groups will almost always have that kind of issue. But some fun scenes and characters. Our story was about a group of people in a mine that had been converted into a fallout shelter just after nuclear war apparently broke out. Supernatural weirdness in the mine (or possibly the mine itself?), taking (mostly) the form of a weird little girl, killed everyone except Jeremy the gentle widower, who in the climax hammered the child in the face and crawled out of the shelter into an ambiguously quiet forest. I was kinda pulling for Antoine, the bodyguard and lover of the older lady whose family had owned the mine, but despite his probably appearing in the most scenes/having the most relationships, he drowned in what seemed to be a literal underground lake of self-doubt.

      \n I had a great time at the Buckets of Dice games convention in Christchurch, New Zealand this weekend.

      We created stories about:
      - a science-fiction author coming out (Left Coast)
      - warriors from the distant future of 2000AD battling lizard invaders with complicated gender identities (Heavy Metal Aeons)
      - a blues magician and his groupies trying to discover where bad luck comes from (Itras By)
      - Roman and British vampires in London, 120AD vying for power (Undying)

      In the boardgame stream, I played (for the first time) 7 Wonders, Roll For the Galaxy, The Castles of Mad King Ludwig, and Forbidden Island.

      Michael Sands and I had very productive conversations about our games in playtest (Left Coast and Heavy Metal Aeons), and I'd expect to see kickstarters for both of those in the near/mid-future.

      We started a new Hillfolk game. Character creation was fun -- I expected it to be a little overwrought from having read the procedures, but it was lighter than I expected and good stuff.
      \nYeah\u2026 I was down on Fae because I thought it cut out all the clarity of Fate Core, all the "if you 're not familiar with Fate, here's how it really works" beginner stuff. But, with Hillfolk, I'd really like a summary book. One person in the group reads the big one, the rest just can read the summary and you gan use the summary as like an unimposing overview.

      \n\nBen_Robbins \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Got together with Marc and Caroline Hobbs (of Downfall fame) for a barrage of playtesting.

      In Marc's game Eden, we learned that bitey little spiders may make bad role-models, but turtles give the worst advice ever. Later we took a new game Caroline's been working on, Entanglement, for a spin. So much difficult romance, so much anime fandom. Vampire-anime fans are brooding, and werewolf-anime fans are intense, but no one understands harpy-anime fans. At all.

      We played Follow and defied my prediction that *no one* would ever want to try the quest where you play doctors curing a disease and argue about ethics and clinical testing. We did and it was fantastic! So\u2026 unexpected achievement unlocked.

      I also played another game of Follow at the Story Games Seattle playtest meetup. Our superheroes tried to get past old grudges and form a team, but our faint hopes went out the window when the 42 year-old career-sidekick's (ordinary) daughter got killed trying to save us from a supervillain. The sidekick was our one voice of unity and optimism and he lost it, naturally.

      And then we kind of nuked part of the city. Quest, failed.

      \n Last night I ran 1%er - The Outlaw Biker Game. The slim book was filled with expletives (there is a stat called "Fucks", as in "I give this many Fucks about doing a thing) that I thought was just a gimmick, but it actually worked into our conversation during play rather well.

      \n This week we continued our long-term campaign in Middle-Earth (using revised FATE 2ed rules with some elements of 3ed and Core). We are playing in 1624 Third Age (few years before The Great Plague) and during the struggle of Arnor against Witch-realm of Angmar. Cardolan is mostly overrun and Arthedain is desperately trying to hold on against onsglauth of orc armies, evil men of Carn D\xfbm, Rhudaur hillmen and Easterlings from afar. Players are now trying to uncover the identity of traitor amongst cardolanian nobles, managed to save kidnapped maid of one of characters (who was mistakenly taken instead of her) and one of characters met long lost cousin from \xc9oth\xe9od... plus there is ancient urul\xf3k\xeb (fire-breathing and flying dragon) who awoke and now is angry and hungry. Oh, boy, I don\xb4t envy my players and their characters a bit.

      We are also playing The Few using play-by-post and African Skies supplement \u2013 players are struggling to repulse Axis attacks against besieged Tobruk, flying desperate missions against Italian and German bombers and fighters... this week Afrikakorps tried to breach the defences in southern sectors using tanks and players managed to destroy some of them with bombs, only to be jumped by German fighters from El Adem in turn. Quiete a show, actually.

      Hey Caesar Slaad that lost Ossuary is fantastic idea thanks for posting, took a bit to get my head around it ):
      \nNo problem.

      Feng Shui Thursdays again this week. I started Red Packet Rumble last week with two players; this time 4 showed up, making the combat a bit more complicated. This time letting the player get away with having their car in the scene worked against them, since the bad guys does as much damage as the more powerful player attack +1.

      And the awakened Dragon has a power that does the enemy's damage +1. So that fight escalated quickly, and the Awekened Dragon was pretty beat up by the end of the ordeal.

      Since we finished early, and I was excited to play with my new toys, I ran a quick Fate Accelerated scenario using It's Not My Fault.

      It was amusing. I mostly banked on D&D tropes, but when I run it again, I may keep different inspirations in the back of my mind.

      We had an Illusionist Con Artist, a Sharpshooter Sorcerer, a Pirate Assassin, and a Barbarian Merchant Performer. Most memorable moments: The Barbarian player did his best Arnie impression hocking wares, and the Sorcerer Sharpshooter played off his area-effect blast as a stream of target-seeknig bullets from his gun a la Zorg's demonstration for the Mangalores in The Fifth Element. They were chasing down a dark elf trickster who conned the merchant out of his wares.

      \n Our Warren game continues. The usual trope is the PCs show up at some new warren where they are unwelcome, or there is an ominous threat kept secret, and I thought - why not subvert that? So Parchmeal's warren welcomed them with open arms as saviors of prophecy and immediately put them in charge. It is its own kind of rabbit hell.

      \n\nAdam_Dray \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n edited June 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I ran the first session of my West Marxist sandbox, The City of Brass. I needed an ongoing game that I could run in a two-hour slot every other week at a cool bar in Baltimore, with the stipulation that players could drop in and play with zero commitment beyond one session. When I asked about D&D stuff that wasn't all murderhoboist, Daniel Levine pointed me at a blog post about adapting West Marches style sandbox play to community-based urban D&D play. So I threw together my City of Brass.

      The PCs are squatters in a collapsing building complex in the worst neighborhood in the city. There are concentric rings of oppression surrounding them, ranging from systemic racism and other bigotry to gang violence to religious zealotry. I am working on a handful of minigame systems to hammer home the oppression.

      Main things right now:

      * Everyone starts with 6 gp.

      * Everyone has a reason to be in the commune and a reason why they can't just leave.

      * Everyone has a profession, something they can try to do to make a living.

      * They live at a poor level, and have to pay 1 sp / day to eat and avoid exhaustion. Per game day, I ask them what they eat, and make them spend 1 sp if they don't have another food source.

      * The building they're squatting in is a wreck, and basically makes everything harder (disadvantage on most rolls). Even getting rest there is hard.

      * The commune as-a-group has five stats based on Maslow's hierarchy of needs. These have low ratings right now, but can be improved through adventures.

      * Once per session, everyone makes a Morale (Wisdom/Insight) check at easy (10) difficulty. Failure means the person must choose one of the five commune stats to lower. "You're bringing the commune down, man."

      I have a random 2d12 table of oppression-based plot hooks. Mostly, these things affect the entire commune, not a single PC. I had the group roll up three of these at the start of play. I wrote each on an index card. They chose what to tackle and how to go about it.

      I figure that solving these problems is the reward mechanism for leveling up. Whenever you take part in the solution of a problem, earn a point. Hard problems might be worth 2 or 3 points. Earn 3 points per level to advance (3 to level to 2nd, 6 to level to 3rd, etc.).
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

    • \n

      Our Warren game continues. The usual trope is the PCs show up at some new warren where they are unwelcome, or there is an ominous threat kept secret, and I thought - why not subvert that? So Parchmeal's warren welcomed them with open arms as saviors of prophecy and immediately put them in charge. It is its own kind of rabbit hell.
      \nVery neat! And I agree about subverting things time to time. When I rotated into the GMs chair the first time around in our Night Witches game, I decided to play against our so-far crapsack world where everyone was out to get the PCs--so I gave them a new Chief of Staff who was willing to fight to protect her pilots and give them what they needed. I wanted to see if I could make a commander the players would want their PCs to follow and die for, since that's a very common war story trope.\n
      I ran the first session of my West Marxist sandbox, The City of Brass. (snip)
      \nThat sounds incredibly awesome :-)

      \n\nmilesgaborit \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n edited June 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n On Saturday night some friends and I got together for some last minute Game Chef playtesting, which was a ton of fun. My dystopian rollerblading RPG, Sun Stealers X-treme, worked pretty much as hoped - lots of wild technology and epic tricks were pulled as we skated past The Corporation's defenses to steal back the sunshine. Said playtesting may have contributed to my staying up until nearly dawn to actually finish my Game Chef submission, but that was a small price to pay.

      Then on Sunday, only mildly zombified from my near-all-nighter, I played in the first session of a Dungeon Crawl Classics game with a group of folks I'd never played with before. The flavor was established early on as "dungeon juvenilia" - frex, the party's goblin thief has a strict rule about only dating goats - which is fine, but I hope it doesn't become the dominant mode of play. I want to not always be silly, you know.

      GM for the new group also dropped the 0-level funnel - unfortunate, as that was one of the main features of DCCRPG that piqued my interest. We didn't get to really see any of the other funny mechanics in play - the elf didn't have any sufficiently crap spellcasting rolls to invoke the corruption/magical misfire rules, and the only character who rolled a fumble was an NPC pet. All in all it felt a lot like the D&D3.5 games I played when I was in my 20s. It was pretty fun, but I'm not sure how long I'll stick around in that game. My gaming dance card is quite full of other interesting stuff (like Blades in the Dark and Apocalypse World this week!) at present.
      \n

      \nKingdom at Story Games Seattle. The royal bloodline of the Witch-Kings of Mennec is tainted, sapping their sorcerous power. They are too weak to take arms against the dragon-worshipping barbarians so our depraved queen turns to the most despised weapon of all\u2026 diplomacy.

      At another meetup we played Follow, but reskinned the "posse" quest as UN investigators hunting down an unshackled AI. We were so busy wondering if we could trust the doctor who had given birth to the AI that we did not foresee the UN's own strike team trying to kill us.

      \nFellowship in which Arkona brought the rest of the Fellowship to the Hatira Elhakile, the Waters of Waking, now a sad and debatable mere. There they fought the Mother of Hydras, traded words with the Overlord Vince the Corrupter, and prevented the creation of Elves 2.0. By the margin of one vote, the Fellowship decided to journey to Turan, the city of Calaf the Heir and defend it from the Blight. Calaf took the bond "I would die for Arkona" and Arkona took the bond "In Calaf one of the great kings of old has returned." Fun!

      Trail of Cthulhu the second version of my scenario. Streamling helped. More to streamline.

      Savage Worlds wait what? but it was returning a visit from some of the nice folks in the local gaming guild. In 1968, a rag tag bunch of Vegas mobsters end up on a spree while just trying to deliver a crooked accountant to his date with a bullet.

      \nCurse of Strahd even longer session (9 hours minus dinner break). The new characters are so far alive. These are the awesomest characters yet.
      One, Gidil, is a gruff, jaded soldier type who started out as a soldier in the Greyhawk wars but took a fiend pact (tome) after one levels and then learned to channel the forces of hell. He is wearing full chain and a shield. His mission from his patron is to make Strahd love Belial.
      The other, Grigor, is wearing a green pinstripe suit, with a bow tie and a purple vest, and a black tophat. He is a theatre director and musician who is traveling with his theatre troupe (actually disguised skeletons, with masks to look like puppets, that he stole from the cemetary and raised from the dead to do the shows). But the skeletons plummeted to their deaths in Ravenloft castle. His mission is to find his stolen lute...(??)

      I usually have all of chapter 6 completely banned (feats and multiclassing) but I opened it up and called it "Summer D&D".

      \n\nmilesgaborit \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Lots of games last week! On Tuesday night played the 3rd-ish session of Curse of Strahd with 6th level characters the group brought over from a previous Ravenloft-like 5th ed. game. So far we've been just lighting up encounters, although we did have a bit of trouble with a group of hags. Fully expect the DM to drop the hammer on us next week.

      On Wednesday I finished up the quickstart scenario for Blades in the Dark with the group-o-twelve-year-olds. Having seen their scheme to rob the Red Sashes' treasury go completely sideways, the kids seized on an opportunity the opposition presented and ignited a bunch of noxious gas, blowing the roof off their targets' hideout. I don't know how much 'heat' that earns them, but it's got to be lots.

      Then, on Friday, played the 2nd session of Apocalypse World, using 2nd edition stuff. We're starting to learn how the disappearances of young women around our settlement may be connected to the psychic maelstrom, and the requisite gang of hungry raiders just appeared on the horizon. Oh, and my character drove a modified 18-wheeler through a flash flood/mud slide, nearly wrecking the truck and surely earning a future beating from its owner. The MC for this game hasn't ever run a PbtA game before - they've mostly run d20/D&D, though they've played in all kinds of games - so there have been a few spots of trouble with fiction-first GMing and their trying to adjust to the permission AW gives you to GO HARD at the characters. Session 2 was better than session 1, so I anticipate session 3 will be more awesome still!
      \n

      \n\nallinonemove \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n edited June 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Started a solo dungeon crawl with a Dungeon World backbone and the Mythic Gamemaster Emulator. Character creation was handled via Goblin Punch career paths and the environs are primarily generated using Perilous Wilds. All of this is being written up using the awesome Trunk Notes personal wiki server on my iPhone.

      Set in early 15th-century alternate Earth, Vojtek Vasely has just entered Zikmund's Spire deep in the woods of central Moldavia in search of a powerful magical component: the Dianthus spiculifolius or \u201cgod flower\u201d.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\n2097 \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n edited June 2016
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n We played Curse of Strahd for the second day in a row, third session this week, but decided against playing tomorrow.
      Somewhere in the Barovia map I had hidden the entirety of Deep Carbon Observatory. A very critically acclaimed module. And the party hadn't find it after a dozen sessions but today they did find it and we started running it. But even after a couple of encounters I was thinking no no no no I hate running these sort of adventures.

      What's the problem? Without spoiling too much, the second part of the module is a river trek. Which, at our table since they're going upriver, pretty much turned into "this happens, then this happens, then this happens". I hate that.

      The first part of the module has a very unconventional structure. I was skeptical towards it but it turned out to work. Not great, but it did work.

      The third part of the module has yet another structure, one I'm more comfortable with but I haven't printed it out or prepped it so I'm glad we wrapped up before we got there (but they almost got there so I better get to work.)

      So, the linear structure of the second part? That's a big problem for me. The second issue is that it's more gross-out horror compared to CoS which more typically has relationship horror or emotional horror.

      And the third issue was that I had decided that the starting event of DCO would happen as soon as the players came to the town where I had hidden it. And, they thought it felt very scripted. During lunch break I explained what was going on, that it wasn't a part of CoS (they thought the very opportune timing of this major event was a part of CoS, where it was just DM mess up in the "glue" between CoS and DCO), that I had decided that this event would happen when they got here and they were like OK, it's cool for sure, we just were angry at CoS but this is an understandable setup now that we know the backstory. (Again transparency of method.)
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n Continued playing Spione. Now our principals are in the thick of it: my HVA spy, whose "cold" is she has exactly zero trust in her handler, was recruited as a double agent by KGB (despite the two agencies supposedly being allies, it looks like the Russians want to keep their East German colleagues on a short leash), while the other guy - an East German worker spying for the West German service West of the wall - was sent to ambush mine and give her a rough time as his initiation ritual to infiltrate a well-connected neo-nazi group (with no knowledge of her actual role as a spy). But no supporting cast have been written out yet, thus I anticipate another 1-2 sessions worth of play before this atrocious mess is over. I'm really liking the game, as expected, despite a few minor quibbles.

      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      I'll be at Dexcon, yes. I am not running City of Brass there, unless you can get it onto the schedule at this late date.
      \nSadly, no influence with such lofty ones as the Masters of Dex. But I have Night Witches Thursday night and Friday afternoon & my Trail scenario on Friday evening.

      Speaking of which...

      Trail of Cthulhu Draft 3 of the scenario, wherein I relegated the excess good ideas to sequels and stripped everything down to basics. This is now much tighter and I'm happy enough with it to go to war.

      Lady Blackbird We had a gender-flipped Captain Cyra Vance, a Lady Blackbird who was shocked, then interested, then intrigued by the idea of what Cyra's attraction to her meant (despite someone pointing out that many of Cornwallis University's students--the Lady went there--were, um, "sapphic until graduation".) Kale's player interpreted the Key of the Mission as meaning he had been hired by Flint to make sure the Lady got to her destination (and this was a pretty dark Kale).

      I usually try to give my players the chance to interact with Captain Hollas (there are so few named NPCs that I assume that Hollas must be important), and as usually happens in those cases, they kidnapped the good Captain. I had great fun sowing discord among the PCs, surprised everyone by having Hollas give his word of honor to protect Lady Blackbird (he knew she was a noblewoman, and once he gave his word he stopped speculating on her identity), and finally had him do a heel-face turn when he confirmed that Vance had abandoned the cruiser Hand of Glory because she wouldn't fire on a refugee ship--the loss of the Glory was revenge taken by the rebels after they pressed the attack (Vance was unable to convince the other captain to break off.)

      It was one of the better Lady Blackbirds I've done :-)

      \n\nLisa Padol \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n We launched the sequel to the Kerberos Fate game I ran a few years back. We're calling it "Machinery of Life", as the PCs consist of Dorian Grey, Dr. Alexander Zachary (like Frankenstein, but takes parenting his creations very seriously), Felicity Sage (child of 2 PCs from previous game -- a shapeshifter and a 9 inch clockwork fairy -- and we've already made the Transformers joke), and Ladon Green (bastard son of the husband of one of the PCs from a previous game, alchemist, plant mage, mother was a dryad).

      We are using Atomic Robo for the base system, which, as Aviatrix noted, can do so many things. I'm not entirely sure how I want to do organizations. We don't think "transportation" quite applies, so I'm tentatively substituting "social" -- letters of credit, introductions, that sort of thing.

      The plot: Dorian Gray wants to join the Kerberos Club and is being a pain about it, so the others need to test him.

      ... and that is how Dorian wound up getting an emu.
      \n

      \n\nAdam_Dray \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I played in my longrunning Pathfinder campaign, where I've been playing my Julie d'Aubigny analog (an ifrit bard 6 / swashbuckler 3 named Julia). She got to burn the faces off some aberrations with searing insults and countersong the maddening caterwaul of some demonic monster.

      I ran the second two-hour installment of my City of Brass "West Marxist" setting for D&D 5e. Social justice issues were generated by rolling on a 2d12 table once per character. They helped one of their commune members deal with the issues of her addiction to spirit potions. They searched for the troublesome, fight-prone brothers who live at the commune, to no avail.

      I've also been prepping for DEXcon this weekend, where I'm running five sessions of Mongoose Traveller (1e). Two sessions of a scenario I've run at TravellerCon, involving the trouble of finding and fixing and purchasing a free trader ship. Three sessions of a totally new Traveller setting based on the American Revolutionary War. In this scenario, they're like Henry Knox and company going off into hinterland Ft. Ticonderoga to fetch 59 cannons that will turn the tide of the battle for NYC against the British fleet, except it's five adventurers flying off to an ice planet to fetch a dozen meson ortillery off a mountain and haul them back to a moon around the New Monhelion planet colony to fight the Noven Kingdom's starship blockade. Good times.

      \n Last week was fairly quiet for me games-wise - but what was lacking in quantity was made up for in quality!

      On Wednesday started a new short arc of The Warren with the group of 12 year olds. One of the kids is trying out being the GM for this one, so I'm just running a character and trying to coach from the sidelines. Character creation was a bit scattered (as is to be expected when it's preteens leading preteens), but everyone was happy with their characters in the end. We got through some leading questions and answers, too, but attention spans waned before we could get into proper play. So the real first session will be this Wednesday.

      Then on Saturday I got to participate in a top secret, by-invitation-only LARP playtest with some of the Olympia, WA game design cabal (this is the QUALITY experience mentioned above). I don't know how many details I'm allowed to divulge, so I'll just say that by the end of the game all players were happy, sweaty, and covered in fake blood. And I got to flex my nearly-atrophied-from-disuse soliloquy muscles! Shakespeare would have been proud.

      \n
      Lisa, Legends of Anglerre was the first time I saw what Fate Core also suggests: do organizations as characters, with aspects and with their own skills.
      Or is the issue more what skill to use? Just add a new one called "dealing with organizations", it's Fate, everything's just words
      \nAtomic Robo Fate uses organizations in place of having a Resources skill, and has rules that fit the comic, for obvious reasons. You can use an organization to analyze something or to get you equipment, and there are rules covering this.

      All well and good -- it's the details I'm trying to chrome out. For Atomic Robo, organizations have 4 skills: Armory (weapons), R&D (devices that aren't weapons or transport), Intel, and Transport,

      For Kerberos Fate, Atomic Robo Remix, the Kerberos Club, not Tesladyne, is the organization the PCs belong to. So:

      Armory -- sure, still applies.
      R&D -- absolutely! Last game, the PCs went to "Radu, the chemist" at the club when they needed weird substances analyzed.
      Intel -- absolutely!

      But, Transport? It's... a little odd. Not impossible, but feels like I'm shoehorning it in.
      But, I want to keep Four things, so as to change as little as possible in the rules. It makes balancing things easier.

      Currently, we're calling it Society, and ruling it provides things like Letters of Credit, Introductions to Certain Famous Personages and Famous, Infamous, and Less Well Known Eccentrics and the like.

      \n A week ago I played nothing but other people's games, this week was the complete opposite.

      We played Kingdom at Story Games Seattle as the Weavers a humanitarian group bent on going back in time and treating the great plagues of history. Our philosophy was that suffering is suffering: it makes no difference if the person has been dead for a thousand years, their pain is just as deserving of treatment as any other patient. We stopped the Black Plague which unintentionally plunged overpopulated Europe into whole new wars. Guesses whether it all went to hell? (yep, we were basically playing a Microscope Echo game of Kingdom)

      As a spur of the moment thing, I also streamed a session of Microscope at the HyperRPG studios. It's actually the very first time I recorded a game of Microscope and it could not have been more fun. Our history was a fantasy analog of climate change: the seasons simply grind to a halt, leaving us in perpetual Autumn, while the rival faerie courts of the Sun and Moon feud and scheme. So much drama! I'll share a link when it gets posted.

      Atomic Robo Fate uses organizations in place of having a Resources skill, and has rules that fit the comic, for obvious reasons. You can use an organization to analyze something or to get you equipment, and there are rules covering this.

      All well and good -- it's the details I'm trying to chrome out. For Atomic Robo, organizations have 4 skills: Armory (weapons), R&D (devices that aren't weapons or transport), Intel, and Transport,

      For Kerberos Fate, Atomic Robo Remix, the Kerberos Club, not Tesladyne, is the organization the PCs belong to. So:

      Armory -- sure, still applies.
      R&D -- absolutely! Last game, the PCs went to "Radu, the chemist" at the club when they needed weird substances analyzed.
      Intel -- absolutely!

      But, Transport? It's... a little odd. Not impossible, but feels like I'm shoehorning it in.
      But, I want to keep Four things, so as to change as little as possible in the rules. It makes balancing things easier.

      Currently, we're calling it Society, and ruling it provides things like Letters of Credit, Introductions to Certain Famous Personages and Famous, Infamous, and Less Well Known Eccentrics and the like.
      \nOh, I didn't understand the mode part! (Still don't -- I find Atomic Robo a little complicated) I searched through the PDF for "organizations" but didn't find anything; but I found that Tesladyne specifically has Armory, R&D, Intel and Transport.
      Society sounds like a good thing to have an organization for.

      \n\nRafu \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      Currently, we're calling it Society, and ruling it provides things like Letters of Credit, Introductions to Certain Famous Personages and Famous, Infamous, and Less Well Known Eccentrics and the like.
      \nIf it was me, I'd call it "Access". Still covers things like getting a letter of credit (if that's what really called for), being received by important people, being allowed into exclusive circles, but also - for example - being allowed into a restricted facility (prison, asylum) or crossing an international border. It also covers means of transportation, should the need ever arise. But, on the other hand, I believe this minimizes overlap with Intel or R&D.

      This was the first time I've seen a love potion end up in the right person, and that person then falling in love with the right person.
      \nThis is such an interesting cocktail, with equal parts tremendously exciting and terribly boring! Fascinating.
      \nIndeed. It was quite exciting in the play however.

      In the third act the viceroy of Venice, one of the villains, seeing that his path to increased power through marriage with the princess was at risk, decided to employ a love potion to shift the princess' attention to himself. While the audience gasped at such villainous behavior he successfully made the princess fall in love with him.

      The spell was later broken and the princess re-united with the count of Verona's nephew, and they were wed in the fifth act. To live happily ever after, presumably.

      \n\nJason_Morningstar \n\n\n

      \n I ran more The Warren last night. The World we're playing in is called Cloverleaf and it is a series of polluted construction sites in between a tangle of highways. Rough sledding all around.

      They found themselves the reluctant-but-loving-it leaders of a messianic cult that expected them to lead the Parchmeal warren to salvation in the care of the Men in White Coats and the Land of Cages. They were living under a freeway overpass (A Deathway, in rabbit parlance) and were sickly and pathetic and overcrowded. It was quite a pickle.

      These cult rabbits reserved a particular hallucinogenic berry for their saviors, and they had briefly tripped previously, so they did it again with a sense of purpose. They'd go to the dreamlands and find an answer to their problem. I made a custom When You Trip Balls move.

      For the dreamlands I went big and mythopoetic, drawing heavily from the Anahuac and the Flowery Dream World. They met Lord Wind amid a landscape of endless trees that never reached the ground; they escaped some snakes, they had a weird conversation with Mother Earth in the darkness, asking her where they could take their warren to that would be safe. She told them life would never be free from danger, and that their "safety" lay in the wombs of their does - their lot in life was to out-breed those that would harm them. They were like "thanks a lot, that's a bummer."

      So they took stock, gave some rousing speeches, and got Parchmeal's warren moving to greener pastures. We used +Marshall Miller's custom move and it was bruuuuuutal:

      When the entire warren relocates, add dice to a pile, one for one, for each statement you can say \u201cyes\u201d to:
      You were once, or still are, a small warren
      But then you were not so small any more
      And in recent years you were very large
      The calamity came without warning
      Your best are away and cannot lead you to safety
      You are being hunted or exterminated
      Parcel out the dice among all the players and have them roll. The total is the number of adult rabbits lost or killed in the great trek. At least one rabbit per die should be a named rabbit. Half the lost will be does, and when a doe dies so do her kits. Remember that rabbits can\u2019t really count.\ufeff

      About 50% of the warren died on the trek, and they are not even done yet.\ufeff

      \nDexcon 2016!

      Night Witches Thursday Night: good way to kick things off. A generally gentle (for NW) session with a bizarre talent show performance that was criticized as being perhaps a bit "formalist."

      Kagematsu in a hack set in Regency Ireland: a lot of fun, although the dice didn't so much betray as stand on top of the hill taunting me and making rude faces. My poor overeducated curate's niece ended up a spinster...in Nova Scotia. And Lord Weymouth failed to protect the village as well.

      Night Witches Friday Night: I used the same set up as Thursday. This game was darker, but props to Rebecca for playing the absolutely most dedicated section leader I've ever seen, and guiding her team through a suicide mission. And they tried to save Lara Nemsteva! Nobody's ever tried to save Lara!

      Trail of Cthulhu: My scenario seemed to work, although the ending needs work. I am finally convinced that I need to cut The Monster from the game. Kill your darlings.

      Fall of Magic: this almost joined Monsterhearts 2015 and Witch 2016 in my "best con games ever" list but fell just a bit short. Props to Darren as Piccolo the Coral Golem, a literal ghost in the shell who brought down the darkness.

      Fellowship: In this installment, we discovered how badly things break when the epic tone of the game gets lost. Fun, but disappointing.

      Masks: In retrospect, Jeff Collyer once again had the best game of the con. It felt a bit disappointing in play, but looking back I think that's because we could sense the immense potential our gang of characters had. My Janus (Wraith/Jenny Delancy) has joined my "characters who need a game" bank.

      Monster of the Week: A fun bit of Lovecraftian shenanigans in the Hudson River Valley. My Spooky descendant of Prospero and Sycorax had fun exasperatedly listening to Scott's very Flaky ideas. (Best one: "There's an anomaly in the region of Saugerties. That's why the Etruscans were there, until the Iroquois Confederacy defeated them using Norse Rune magic." Runner up: "Well, sure, that Vatican. Actually, we can eliminate all seven Vaticans.")

      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJuly 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Let me think on it. In brief, some of the players struggled at first to go for the full-throat epicness of the Long Journey sequence; an attempt by Jeff to pull us back on course after a break backfired, unintentionally I guess, and Jeff being the excellent GM he is followed the players. Mostly there were a few issues making some political analogues as commentary on moves (we were joking around about convincing a guardian spirit to take its accumulated vacation time and go look for work with some nomads) that spun out into anarchist dwarves (this was a bit offensive to one of the players, a no-kidding anarchist who had been in Seattle during WTO) and ultimately collapsed with the introduction of the titan Bernardus Sanderson. (Le sigh.)

      I mean...up until that last bit, it wasn't a case of any single thing breaking tone beyond repair, just a snowballing of tone breaks that spun the game out of any hope of regaining tone.

      We had a similar issue a few times in Fall of Magic (at least from where I was sitting), so it is much on my mind, especially since I consider one of the few areas of authority I keep as GM is to be a guardian of tone: not in an imposing way, more in a "let's try to steer back to where we agreed to be" way. Of course, most of my long-form GMing over the last two years has been Trail of Cthulhu, and while I have my own spin on my reboot-heavy stuff ("Buffystar Galactica" sums it up), that doesn't mean that I won't try and push back gently against too much comedy.

      So yeah, more than this probably deserves a thread on tone maintenance in general, as I have other thoughts on that.

      \n\nMel_White \n\n\n

      \nMore Dexcon 2016!

      Noir World. John Adamus\u2019 game in development does nice things with hooks as expanded bonds from PbtA type games to really create the feel for an environment where the characters have long-term, existing relationships with each other that take precedence over a particular mystery or crime that is the ostensible focus of the adventure.

      Traveller. Played Adam Dray\u2019s \u201cFree Trader\u201d scenario, which is all about finding and putting a ship into operation. Needless to say, we never even really found a ship. But what a blast! Great table of players meant even our failures were entertaining.

      Night\u2019s Black Agents. Ran a variant of my brother, Bill\u2019s, \u201cLazarus Sanction\u201d scenario. In my version, the supernatural, oil politics, and the European F1 race mix it up in Baku!

      With Great Power. Ran the new version for the first time. Learned again that in any GMless game it is really necessary to build a shared expectation of the game in the first few minutes of play. WGP does this in an \u201chomage\u201d to superheroes at the start, but only if everyone is listening hard!

      Trail of Cthulhu. Got to play a pedantic Miskatonic professor. Modeled a little on Bill\u2026maybe? A bit frustrating because it seemed hard to get off the script but I survived with my sanity and tenure, so not bad!

      Clash of the Five Kingdoms, a Fate Core variant by Dave Petroski, playing nation-states instead of individual characters. My wizards of Arkady stopped the invading hordes of Badoom, admittedly after their momentum had been broken by the Wandering Circus, a nomadic people. Reminded me of TSR\u2019s old Divine Right game!

      \n\nGuy Srinivasan \n\n\n

      \n\nJuly 2016 \n

      \nAnima Prime. Just did world and character creation. World is post-apocalyptic steampunk anime, the globe was an egg full of dragons that hatched when it passed through an area of space with particularly weak walls between this dimension and the Krell (hell krill) dimension. Now most of the world's surface is floating islands that usually stay floating, the dragons ate their fill and flew away, and demon shrimp still come through portals to plague the wrecked land. Will we save our homeland? The world? Each other?

      We:
      * Old, old, man with a strange electricity affinity
      * 12-year-old kid whose imaginary friends are real
      * https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E\xf6l raised by wolves
      * Visionary healer scientist
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nBen_Robbins \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJuly 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Double playtests of the new version of Follow. The first one was great, an unexpected mix of suburban family life and cyberpunk netrunning that turned out surprisingly good ("You can take down corporate America after you finish your homework!" "Awwwww, Mommmmm!")

      The second game was\u2026 just wow. Totally intense. Super-real in the best possible way. The whole table was all-in. We had to keep taking breaks to let everyone cool down from the dramatic tension. I haven't been able to write it up properly yet because it was so hot.

      So, a very good week.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nBen_Robbins \n\n\n

      \n\nJuly 2016 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      As a spur of the moment thing, I also streamed a session of Microscope at the HyperRPG studios. It's actually the very first time I recorded a game of Microscope and it could not have been more fun. Our history was a fantasy analog of climate change: the seasons simply grind to a halt, leaving us in perpetual Autumn, while the rival faerie courts of the Sun and Moon feud and scheme. So much drama! I'll share a link when it gets posted.
      \nOh and the video for this game is up: Winter Is Not Coming.

      There's a lot of chat with the audience at the start, because of the format of the show. The game proper starts about 45 minutes in and around 1:30 we start the glorious "Death of the Sun Queen" arc.

      Dracula Dossier 1940 Joyce pilots a boat from Castle Dracula to the Bucharest region to avoid the machinations of Carmilla. Meanwhile, just what's up with the re-burying of one of the founders of the Iron Guard? Can the undead be involved? And shouldn't they just be trying to finish their exfil to Belgrade instead?
      \nLogically, of course, they should. But, at least two of the others feel they owe aid on the matter of vanishing people, and at least one, possibly as many as three, as Quimby put it, want "to see Dracula drinking Nazi blood".

      \n
      We used +Marshall Miller's custom move and it was bruuuuuutal:

      When the entire warren relocates, add dice to a pile, one for one, for each statement you can say \u201cyes\u201d to:
      You were once, or still are, a small warren
      But then you were not so small any more
      And in recent years you were very large
      The calamity came without warning
      Your best are away and cannot lead you to safety
      You are being hunted or exterminated
      Parcel out the dice among all the players and have them roll. The total is the number of adult rabbits lost or killed in the great trek. At least one rabbit per die should be a named rabbit. Half the lost will be does, and when a doe dies so do her kits. Remember that rabbits can\u2019t really count.\ufeff

      About 50% of the warren died on the trek, and they are not even done yet.\ufeff
      \nJebus. Ow. OW. (I love it.)
